### Post by ~LoKe on 2008-02-29
March 2008 Desktops - Posting Guidelines

* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.

* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.

* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.

* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.

* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.

* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.

*To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

---

### Post by lzfy on 2008-02-29
Quoting from last months thread.
> **p_quarles said:**
> +1

I use mostly KDE applications (not KWin, though), and appreciate the value of a consistent theme. Since it's easier to get Gtk apps to mimic a Qt theme than vice versa*, I use QtCurve and attempt to make it as minimalist as possible. I'm very happy with it, but would be delighted to find a Qt style that let me get rid of some of the extraneous glitter.

I know this can be done, it just hasn't yet. 

* If I'm wrong about this, please: someone tell me.

[This]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Skulpture?content=59031") looks very promising. But it looks like it's for KDE4.

### Post by macogw on 2008-03-01
> **~LoKe said:**
> I'm leaving in about 8 days so I have to set up my computer for my brother, so he can easily burn the movies I have. :(

Setup a user account for him with a simple UI (you can use a program called Sabayon to configure GNOME for other users without logging out) and then make a group, maybe called "movies" and put yourselves both in it.  Then chown the directory of movies so that the group is "movies" and he has access.  Then give him a nice symlink on his desktop to the directory.

### Post by Gigamo on 2008-03-01

---

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-03-01
> **Gigamo said:**
> PurpuseofReason, could you give me all your font settings?

I just switched to Arch, everything is working (even awesomewm :D) except sound, but fonts look a bit different than on ubuntu with the same settings.
You'll need special font packages. If you ask the arch forums, they'll say "read the wiki", I'll just send you to it. ;)

[http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Fonts#Beautify_Fonts_for_LCD_in_X](http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Fonts#Beautify_Fonts_for_LCD_in_X)

The wiki really does have everything. :) A quick howto for the AUR, because I know it's a new concept and you'll need it for this, you look up a package in the AUR and download it's tarball. Extract it and cd into the folder with a terminal and type makepkg. It will either make the package or say you need some dependicies (get them if you need them with pacman -S). When it is done, you will be able to, as root, pacman -U *.pkg.tar.gz in install it. U means local install if you were wondering. Which arch did you install (i686 or x86_64)?

For sound (I know this is off topic) what have you done and what is your sound card?

EDIT - Because you're using no DE, make sure your gtkrc file reflects what font to use etc.

### Post by herbster on 2008-03-01
> **cawill said:**
> Nice desktop.
Could you post your .screenrc please?

```
startup_message off
vbell           off
defscrollback   5000
shell           -$SHELL
shelltitle      sh
autodetach      on
altscreen on

escape ``

termcapinfo rxvt ti@:te@
bindkey "^[q" prev
bindkey "^[w" next

screen -t irssi 8 irssi
screen -t shell 0
screen -t htop 9 htop
select 0

hardstatus alwayslastline
hardstatus string '%{= Y}[%{w}%H%{Y}][%{w}%=%?%-Lw%?%{Y}%n*%f%t%?(%u)%? %{w}%?%+Lw%?%?%=%{Y}][%{w}%m/%d %{W}%C%A%{Y}]'

backtick 100 5 5 tail -1 /var/tmp/vermaden-stats-top
#caption always '%{= wk} %= %100` %='

shelltitle "$ | bash"
```

---

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-03-03
> **Linuturk said:**
> I'm an arch guy too. Can you post your info script? Mine hasn't worked right for a while, and I'd like to compare my code.
As an arch user, I'll post mine.
```

#!/usr/bin/perl
use Switch;

use strict;

####################
## Config options ##
####################

## What distro logo to use to use, Available "Archlinux Debian None" ##
my $distro = "Archlinux";

## what values to display. Use "OS Kernel DE WM win_theme Theme Font Icons" ##
my $display = "OS Kernel DE WM Win_theme Wallpaper Theme Icons Font";

## Takes a screen shot if set to 0 ##
my $shot = 0;
## Command to run to take screen shot ##
my $command = "scrot '%m.%d.%Y-shot.png' -d 5";

## What colors to use for the variables. ##
my $textcolor = "\e[0m";

## Prints little debugging messages if set to 0 ##
my $quite = 0;

########################
## Script starts here ##
########################
## Define some thing to work with strict ##
my @line = ();
my $found = 0;
my $DE = "NONE";
my $WM = "NONE";

## Hash of WMs and the process they run ##
my %WMlist = ("Beryl", "beryl",
	      "Compiz", "compiz",
              "Fluxbox", "fluxbox",
              "Openbox", "openbox",
              "Blackbox", "blackbox",
              "Xfwm4", "xfwm4",
              "Metacity", "metacity",
              "Kwin", "kwin",
              "FVWM", "fvwm",
              "Enlightenment", "enlightenment",
              "IceWM", "icewm",
              "Window Maker", "wmaker",
	      "AwesomeWM", "awesomewm",
              "PekWM","pekwm" );

## Hash of DEs and the process they run ##     
my %DElist = ("Gnome", "gnome-session",
              "Xfce4", "xfce-mcs-manage",
              "KDE", "ksmserver");

## Get Kernel version ##
if ( $display =~ "Kernel"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Kernel version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $kernel = `uname -r`;
  $kernel =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $kernel = " Kernel:$textcolor $kernel";
  push(@line, "$kernel");
}

## Find running processes ##
print "\::$textcolor Getting processes \n" unless $quite == 1;
my $processes = `ps -A | awk {'print \$4'}`;

## Find DE ##
while( (my $DEname, my $DEprocess) = each(%DElist) ) {
  print "\::$textcolor Testing $DEname process: $DEprocess \n" unless $quite == 1;
  if ( $processes =~ m/$DEprocess/ ) {
    $DE = $DEname;
    print "\::$textcolor DE found as $DE\n" unless $quite == 1;
    if( $display =~ m/DE/ ) {
      push(@line, " DE:$textcolor $DE");
    }
    last;
  }
}

## Find WM ##
while( (my $WMname, my $WMprocess) = each(%WMlist) ) {
 print "\::$textcolor Testing $WMname process: $WMprocess \n" unless $quite == 1;
  if ( $processes =~ m/$WMprocess/ ) {
    $WM = $WMname;
    print "\::$textcolor WM found as $WM\n" unless $quite == 1;
    if( $display =~ m/WM/ ) {
      push(@line, " WM:$textcolor $WM");
    }
    last;
  }
}

## Find WM theme ##
if ( $display =~ m/Win_theme/ ){
  switch($WM) {
    case "Openbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/openbox/rc.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /<name>(.+)<\/name>/ ) {
          while ( $found == 0 ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
            $found = 1;
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Compiz" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.emerald/themes/Elegant/theme.ini")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /name=(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Metacity" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /apps/metacity/general/theme`;
      print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $gconf\n" unless $quite == 1;
      chomp ($gconf);
      push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $gconf");
    }
    case "Fluxbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.fluxbox/init")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /session.styleFile:.*\/(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Blackbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.blackboxrc")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /session.styleFile:.*\/(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Xfwm4" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/xfwm4.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /<option name="Xfwm\/ThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
  } 
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Kwin" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.kde/share/config/kwinrc")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /PluginLib=kwin3_(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Enlightenment" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      my $remote = `enlightenment_remote -theme-get theme` ;
      if( $remote =~ m/.*FILE="(.+).edj"/ ) {
        print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
        push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
      }     
    }       
    case "IceWM" { 
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.icewm/theme")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /Theme="(.+)\/.*.theme/ ) {
          while( $found == 0 ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
            $found = 1;
          }
        }
      }   
      close(FILE);
    }   
    case "PekWM" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.pekwm/config")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /Theme.*\/(.*)"/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE); 
    } 
  }   
}     
      
## Find Theme Icon ans Font ##
if ( $display =~ m/[Theme, Icons, Font, Wallpaper]/) {
  switch($DE) {
    case "Gnome" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/gtk_theme`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        print "\::$textcolor GTK Theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
        push(@line, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $gconf");
      }
      if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/icon_theme`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $gconf");
      } 
      if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/font_name`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $gconf");
      }
    } 
    case "Xfce4" {
      my @sort = ();
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/gtk.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
     if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
          if (/<option name="Net\/ThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor GTK Theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
          if (/<option name="Net\/IconThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
          if ( /<option name="Gtk\/FontName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Font found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " Font:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
      ## Sort variables so they're ordered "Theme Icon Font" ##
      foreach my $i (@sort) {
        push(@line, "$i");
      }
open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/desktop.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if ( $display =~ m/Wallpaper/ ) {
          if ( /<option name="imagepath_0_0" type="string" value=".*\/(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\:: Wallpaper found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Wallpaper:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    } 
    case "KDE" { 
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.kde/share/config/kdeglobals")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) { 
        if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
          if ( /widgetStyle=(.+)/  ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Wiget Style found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Wiget Style:$textcolor $1");
          }
          if (/colorScheme=(.+).kcsrc/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Color Scheme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Color Scheme:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
          if ( /Theme=(.+)/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }   
        if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
          if ( /font=(.+)/ ) {
            my $font = (split/,/, $1)[0];
            print "\::$textcolor Font found as $font\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $font");
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    else {
      my @files = ("$ENV{HOME}/.gtkrc-2.0", "$ENV{HOME}/.gtkrc.mine",);
      foreach my $file (@files) {
        if ( -e $file ) {
          print "\::$textcolor Opening $file\n" unless $quite == 1; 
          open(FILE, $file)
          || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
          while( <FILE> ) {
            if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
              if( /include ".*themes\/(.+)\/gtk-(1|2)\.0\/gtkrc"/ ){
                print "\::$textcolor GTK theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $1");
              }
            }
            if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
              if( /.*gtk-icon-theme-name.*"(.+)"/ ) {
                print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
              }
            }
            if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
              if( /.*gtk-font-name.*"(.+)"/ ) {
                print "\::$textcolor Font found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $1");
             }
            }
          }
          close(FILE);
        }
      }
    }
  }
}

## Display the system info ##
if ( $distro =~ m/Archlinux/ ) {

## Get Archlinux version ##
if ( $display =~ "OS"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Archlinux version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $version = `cat /etc/arch-release`;
  $version =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $version = " OS:$textcolor $version";
  unshift(@line, "$version");
}

my $c1 = "\e[1;37m";
my $c2 = "\e[0;34m";

print "$c1
$c1               +             
$c1               A             
$c1              RCH               $c2@line[0]
$c1             ARCHA              $c2@line[1]
$c1             RCHARC             $c2@line[2]
$c1            ; HARCH;            $c2@line[3] 
$c1           +AR.CHARC            $c2@line[4]
$c1          +HARCHARCHA           $c2@line[5]
$c1         RCHARC$c2\HARCH$c1\AR;         $c2@line[6]    
$c1        CHA$c2\RCHARCHARCHA$c1+        $c2@line[7]    
$c1       R$c2\CHARCH   ARCHARC        $c2@line[8]   
$c2     .HARCHA;     ;RCH;`\".     $c2@line[9]
$c2    .ARCHARC;     ;HARCH.   
$c2    ARCHARCHA.   .RCHARCHA`     
$c2   RCHARC'           'HARCHA   
$c2  ;RCHA                 RCHA; 
$c2  RC'                     'HA 
$c2 R'                         `C
$c2'                            ` 
\e[0m";
}


if ( $distro =~ m/None/ ) {
my $color = "\e[0;34m";
  foreach my $filled ( @line ) {
    print "$color $filled\n"
  }
}

if ( $distro =~ m/Debian/ ) {

## Get Debian version ##
if ( $display =~ "OS"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Debian version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $version = `cat /etc/Debian_release`;
  $version =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $version = " OS:$textcolor $version";
  unshift(@line, "$version");
}
my $c1 = "\e[0;31m";

print "
$c1       _,met\$\$\$\$\$gg.
$c1    ,g\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$P.
$c1  ,g\$\$P\"\"       \"\"\"Y\$\$.\".              @line[0]
$c1 ,\$\$P'              \`\$\$\$.              @line[1]
$c1',\$\$P       ,ggs.     \`\$\$b:            @line[2]
$c1\`d\$\$'     ,\$P\"'   .    \$\$\$             @line[3]
$c1 \$\$P      d\$'     ,    \$\$P             @line[4]
$c1 \$\$:      \$\$.   -    ,d\$\$'             @line[5]
$c1 \$\$\;      Y\$b._   _,d\$P'               @line[6]
$c1 Y\$\$.    \`.\`\"Y\$\$\$\$P\"'                  @line[7]
$c1 \`\$\$b      \"-.__                       @line[8]
$c1  \`Y\$\$
$c1   \`Y\$\$.
$c1     \`\$\$b.
$c1       \`Y\$\$b.
$c1          \`\"Y\$b._
$c1              \`\"\"\"\"
\e[0m";   
}       

     
## Run screen shot graper ##
`$command` unless $shot != 0;

```

### Post by Linuturk on 2008-03-03
> **PurposeOfReason said:**
> As an arch user, I'll post mine.
```

#!/usr/bin/perl
use Switch;

use strict;

####################
## Config options ##
####################

## What distro logo to use to use, Available "Archlinux Debian None" ##
my $distro = "Archlinux";

## what values to display. Use "OS Kernel DE WM win_theme Theme Font Icons" ##
my $display = "OS Kernel DE WM Win_theme Wallpaper Theme Icons Font";

## Takes a screen shot if set to 0 ##
my $shot = 0;
## Command to run to take screen shot ##
my $command = "scrot '%m.%d.%Y-shot.png' -d 5";

## What colors to use for the variables. ##
my $textcolor = "\e[0m";

## Prints little debugging messages if set to 0 ##
my $quite = 0;

########################
## Script starts here ##
########################
## Define some thing to work with strict ##
my @line = ();
my $found = 0;
my $DE = "NONE";
my $WM = "NONE";

## Hash of WMs and the process they run ##
my %WMlist = ("Beryl", "beryl",
	      "Compiz", "compiz",
              "Fluxbox", "fluxbox",
              "Openbox", "openbox",
              "Blackbox", "blackbox",
              "Xfwm4", "xfwm4",
              "Metacity", "metacity",
              "Kwin", "kwin",
              "FVWM", "fvwm",
              "Enlightenment", "enlightenment",
              "IceWM", "icewm",
              "Window Maker", "wmaker",
	      "AwesomeWM", "awesomewm",
              "PekWM","pekwm" );

## Hash of DEs and the process they run ##     
my %DElist = ("Gnome", "gnome-session",
              "Xfce4", "xfce-mcs-manage",
              "KDE", "ksmserver");

## Get Kernel version ##
if ( $display =~ "Kernel"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Kernel version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $kernel = `uname -r`;
  $kernel =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $kernel = " Kernel:$textcolor $kernel";
  push(@line, "$kernel");
}

## Find running processes ##
print "\::$textcolor Getting processes \n" unless $quite == 1;
my $processes = `ps -A | awk {'print \$4'}`;

## Find DE ##
while( (my $DEname, my $DEprocess) = each(%DElist) ) {
  print "\::$textcolor Testing $DEname process: $DEprocess \n" unless $quite == 1;
  if ( $processes =~ m/$DEprocess/ ) {
    $DE = $DEname;
    print "\::$textcolor DE found as $DE\n" unless $quite == 1;
    if( $display =~ m/DE/ ) {
      push(@line, " DE:$textcolor $DE");
    }
    last;
  }
}

## Find WM ##
while( (my $WMname, my $WMprocess) = each(%WMlist) ) {
 print "\::$textcolor Testing $WMname process: $WMprocess \n" unless $quite == 1;
  if ( $processes =~ m/$WMprocess/ ) {
    $WM = $WMname;
    print "\::$textcolor WM found as $WM\n" unless $quite == 1;
    if( $display =~ m/WM/ ) {
      push(@line, " WM:$textcolor $WM");
    }
    last;
  }
}

## Find WM theme ##
if ( $display =~ m/Win_theme/ ){
  switch($WM) {
    case "Openbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/openbox/rc.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /<name>(.+)<\/name>/ ) {
          while ( $found == 0 ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
            $found = 1;
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Compiz" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.emerald/themes/Elegant/theme.ini")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /name=(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Metacity" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /apps/metacity/general/theme`;
      print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $gconf\n" unless $quite == 1;
      chomp ($gconf);
      push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $gconf");
    }
    case "Fluxbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.fluxbox/init")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /session.styleFile:.*\/(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Blackbox" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.blackboxrc")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /session.styleFile:.*\/(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Xfwm4" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/xfwm4.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /<option name="Xfwm\/ThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
  } 
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Kwin" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.kde/share/config/kwinrc")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /PluginLib=kwin3_(.+)/ ) {
          print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
          push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    case "Enlightenment" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      my $remote = `enlightenment_remote -theme-get theme` ;
      if( $remote =~ m/.*FILE="(.+).edj"/ ) {
        print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
        push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
      }     
    }       
    case "IceWM" { 
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.icewm/theme")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /Theme="(.+)\/.*.theme/ ) {
          while( $found == 0 ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
            $found = 1;
          }
        }
      }   
      close(FILE);
    }   
    case "PekWM" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $WM theme\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.pekwm/config")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if( /Theme.*\/(.*)"/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor $WM theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " WM Theme:$textcolor $1");
        }
      }
      close(FILE); 
    } 
  }   
}     
      
## Find Theme Icon ans Font ##
if ( $display =~ m/[Theme, Icons, Font, Wallpaper]/) {
  switch($DE) {
    case "Gnome" {
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/gtk_theme`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        print "\::$textcolor GTK Theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
        push(@line, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $gconf");
      }
      if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/icon_theme`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $gconf");
      } 
      if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
        my $gconf = `gconftool-2 -g /desktop/gnome/interface/font_name`;
        chomp ($gconf);
        push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $gconf");
      }
    } 
    case "Xfce4" {
      my @sort = ();
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/gtk.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
     if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
          if (/<option name="Net\/ThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor GTK Theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
          if (/<option name="Net\/IconThemeName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
          if ( /<option name="Gtk\/FontName" type="string" value="(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Font found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            unshift(@sort, " Font:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
      ## Sort variables so they're ordered "Theme Icon Font" ##
      foreach my $i (@sort) {
        push(@line, "$i");
      }
open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.config/xfce4/mcs_settings/desktop.xml")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) {
        if ( $display =~ m/Wallpaper/ ) {
          if ( /<option name="imagepath_0_0" type="string" value=".*\/(.+)"\/>/ ) {
            print "\:: Wallpaper found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Wallpaper:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    } 
    case "KDE" { 
      print "\::$textcolor Finding $DE variables\n" unless $quite == 1;
      open(FILE, "$ENV{HOME}/.kde/share/config/kdeglobals")
      || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
      while( <FILE> ) { 
        if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
          if ( /widgetStyle=(.+)/  ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Wiget Style found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Wiget Style:$textcolor $1");
          }
          if (/colorScheme=(.+).kcsrc/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Color Scheme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Color Scheme:$textcolor $1");
          }
        }
        if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
          if ( /Theme=(.+)/ ) {
            print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
          } 
        }   
        if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
          if ( /font=(.+)/ ) {
            my $font = (split/,/, $1)[0];
            print "\::$textcolor Font found as $font\n" unless $quite == 1;
            push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $font");
          }
        }
      }
      close(FILE);
    }
    else {
      my @files = ("$ENV{HOME}/.gtkrc-2.0", "$ENV{HOME}/.gtkrc.mine",);
      foreach my $file (@files) {
        if ( -e $file ) {
          print "\::$textcolor Opening $file\n" unless $quite == 1; 
          open(FILE, $file)
          || die "\e[0;31m<Failed>\n";
          while( <FILE> ) {
            if ( $display =~ m/Theme/ ) {
              if( /include ".*themes\/(.+)\/gtk-(1|2)\.0\/gtkrc"/ ){
                print "\::$textcolor GTK theme found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " GTK Theme:$textcolor $1");
              }
            }
            if ( $display =~ m/Icons/ ) {
              if( /.*gtk-icon-theme-name.*"(.+)"/ ) {
                print "\::$textcolor Icons found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " Icons:$textcolor $1");
              }
            }
            if ( $display =~ m/Font/ ) {
              if( /.*gtk-font-name.*"(.+)"/ ) {
                print "\::$textcolor Font found as $1\n" unless $quite == 1;
                push(@line, " Font:$textcolor $1");
             }
            }
          }
          close(FILE);
        }
      }
    }
  }
}

## Display the system info ##
if ( $distro =~ m/Archlinux/ ) {

## Get Archlinux version ##
if ( $display =~ "OS"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Archlinux version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $version = `cat /etc/arch-release`;
  $version =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $version = " OS:$textcolor $version";
  unshift(@line, "$version");
}

my $c1 = "\e[1;37m";
my $c2 = "\e[0;34m";

print "$c1
$c1               +             
$c1               A             
$c1              RCH               $c2@line[0]
$c1             ARCHA              $c2@line[1]
$c1             RCHARC             $c2@line[2]
$c1            ; HARCH;            $c2@line[3] 
$c1           +AR.CHARC            $c2@line[4]
$c1          +HARCHARCHA           $c2@line[5]
$c1         RCHARC$c2\HARCH$c1\AR;         $c2@line[6]    
$c1        CHA$c2\RCHARCHARCHA$c1+        $c2@line[7]    
$c1       R$c2\CHARCH   ARCHARC        $c2@line[8]   
$c2     .HARCHA;     ;RCH;`\".     $c2@line[9]
$c2    .ARCHARC;     ;HARCH.   
$c2    ARCHARCHA.   .RCHARCHA`     
$c2   RCHARC'           'HARCHA   
$c2  ;RCHA                 RCHA; 
$c2  RC'                     'HA 
$c2 R'                         `C
$c2'                            ` 
\e[0m";
}


if ( $distro =~ m/None/ ) {
my $color = "\e[0;34m";
  foreach my $filled ( @line ) {
    print "$color $filled\n"
  }
}

if ( $distro =~ m/Debian/ ) {

## Get Debian version ##
if ( $display =~ "OS"){
  print "\::$textcolor Finding Debian version\n" unless $quite == 1;
  my $version = `cat /etc/Debian_release`;
  $version =~ s/\s+/ /g;
  $version = " OS:$textcolor $version";
  unshift(@line, "$version");
}
my $c1 = "\e[0;31m";

print "
$c1       _,met\$\$\$\$\$gg.
$c1    ,g\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$\$P.
$c1  ,g\$\$P\"\"       \"\"\"Y\$\$.\".              @line[0]
$c1 ,\$\$P'              \`\$\$\$.              @line[1]
$c1',\$\$P       ,ggs.     \`\$\$b:            @line[2]
$c1\`d\$\$'     ,\$P\"'   .    \$\$\$             @line[3]
$c1 \$\$P      d\$'     ,    \$\$P             @line[4]
$c1 \$\$:      \$\$.   -    ,d\$\$'             @line[5]
$c1 \$\$\;      Y\$b._   _,d\$P'               @line[6]
$c1 Y\$\$.    \`.\`\"Y\$\$\$\$P\"'                  @line[7]
$c1 \`\$\$b      \"-.__                       @line[8]
$c1  \`Y\$\$
$c1   \`Y\$\$.
$c1     \`\$\$b.
$c1       \`Y\$\$b.
$c1          \`\"Y\$b._
$c1              \`\"\"\"\"
\e[0m";   
}       

     
## Run screen shot graper ##
`$command` unless $shot != 0;
```

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-03-03
> **xhhux said:**
> thanks, its a Firefox plugin, called no menu, i think  :)

Hide Menubar, I just installed it.

Note: do NOT use the "personal menu" extension if you plan on hiding the top menu. For some stupid reason, when you hide the top menu with that extension installed, it puts all the text OF the top menu crammed into the far left of the Navigation menu. I have no idea why, it might just be a 3.0b3 thing, but it's very, very annoying.

### Post by RebounD11 on 2008-03-04
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Could you please post the script it seems you used to show that bar with the elapsed time of the track playing on Audacious?

Thanks in advance.


Yes I can... but like I said it's kind of barbaric... I am a very very poor coder, and I don't like bothering my girlfriend with stuff like this... she has more important stuff to take care of.

Anyway here it it:

```

#!/bin/bash

CURRENT=`(set \`audtool current-song-output-length-seconds\`; echo $1)`
MAX=`(set \`audtool current-song-length-seconds\`; echo $1)`

k=$(($CURRENT * 100 / $MAX ))

echo $k

```

I tried to put it in /usr/bin... to launch it from anywhere, but it didn't work like that.

EDIT: You're welcome! :D God I'm a wreck when I need to go to school early in the morning.

### Post by ayoli on 2008-03-05
> **notwen said:**
> Anyway I could modify this to locate my Intel X3100 chipset, instead of a nVidia card?  =]

Replace this line :
```
echo -e " GPU:            $gras$(cat /proc/driver/nvidia/cards/0 | grep Model | cut --delimiter=" " -f3,4,5,6,7,8,9)$fin"
```
with this :
```
echo -e "Graphics: $gras$(lspci |grep 00:02.1 |cut --delimiter=" " -f 4,5,6,7,8,9)$fin"
```

edit: you may need to adjust the pci address (00:02.1) to match your X3100.

---

### Post by notwen on 2008-03-05
> **ayoli said:**
> Replace this line :
```
echo -e " GPU:            $gras$(cat /proc/driver/nvidia/cards/0 | grep Model | cut --delimiter=" " -f3,4,5,6,7,8,9)$fin"
memtotal=$((`grep "MemTotal" /proc/meminfo|cut -c 12-22|indent -i0`/1024))
```
with this :
```
echo -e "Graphics: $gras$(lspci |grep 00:02.1 |cut --delimiter=" " -f 4,5,6,7,8,9)"
```

edit: you may need to adjust the pci address (00:02.1) to match your X3100.

Thank you very much, lspci was the only way I knew to output my Graphics card, but I was not sure of what to cut.  I'll be sure to test the output when I get home.  =]

[img]http://ogunderground.com/random/workstation/screenshots/info_files/dec.png[/img] **Emerald Theme**: Posi (modified)
[img]http://ogunderground.com/random/workstation/screenshots/info_files/font.png[/img] **Fonts**: Sans, best contrast smoothing
[img]http://ogunderground.com/random/workstation/screenshots/info_files/gtk.png[/img] **GTK Theme**: MurrineTango, with Tango icons (newest updates)
[img]http://ogunderground.com/random/workstation/screenshots/info_files/cf.png[/img] **C-F Plugins**: Expo, Wallpaper, Cube (-Rotate, -Reflections), 3d Windows, Magnifier, Ezoom, Scale, Window Previews, Show Mouse, Animations
[img]Expo, Wallpaper, Cube (-Rotate, -Reflections), 3d Windows, Wiitrack (my plugin), Magnifier, Ezoom, Scale, Window Previews, Show Mouse, Animations[/img] **Screenlets**: System Monitor, ClearWeather (modified), ClearCalendar.

**Other goodies**:
CCSM, WICD, Screenlets-Manager and Nautilus - I added RGBA colormap support to all of them (Nautilus and WICD have some bugs, WICD's main window doesn't have the RGBA support, and the Gnome foot in Nautilus has a solid background) I also have the RGBA plugin running in Gedit.

**Edit**: Just hacked up Pidgin to do it. Doesn't work on the buddy list (probably because of where I set the colormap), and you have to open a tab to get it to work on the chat window, but overall, it's pretty nice.

### Post by koleoptero on 2008-03-05
> **arbulus said:**
> I see you're using Exaile.  What do you think of it?  I used it maybe 6 months ago and it was really crashy.  I have a fairly large music library (~50GB) so I didn't know if maybe it had trouble with such large libraries.  Does it work well for you? I'm using exaile too for this reason. Amarok is better but I can't stand it when using a dark theme. Exaile is in general a bit heavier memory-wise, and a little slower when starting up, but other than that works fine. It has a few bugs but they're minor. Of course the slow startup and large memory takeup (~120MB ram) is because I have 20.000 songs, about 150GB of music. But it's the only one that has an equaliser, a decent library and works for me.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-03-06
> **sunexplodes said:**
> Looking at the screenshot a few pages back, it just looks to me like the inactive window has a different opacity setting than the active window does in the Emerald Configuration, which would explain the difference in colour. If you open the Emerald Control Panel and change both active AND inactive windows to have NO opacity, does that solve the problem?

Actually, both the active and the inactive windows' titles have the same colour, only the text is different. What is happening here is that each person is having problems with the way their computers are rendering the GTK and the Metacity themes. In my case, all the colours of Elegant Brit's GTK version are slightly darker than they should... And it's so weird, because all the theme's files and pixmaps are correct.


Anyway, your screenshot is awesome. Either on QT or on GTK, the results are always great...

### Post by triphazard on 2008-03-08
Just started out on OpenBox and got it set up quite nicely now.  Here are the details: -

**Wallpaper:** [Here]("http://wallpaper.skins.be/alessandra-ambrosio/23876/1680x1050/")
**OpenBox:** [Lily theme@box-look.org]("http://http://box-look.org/content/show.php/Lily?content=61376")
**GTK:** [Lily@gnome-look.org]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Lily?content=53635")
**Conky:** [Conky Scripts@gnome-look.org]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Conky+scripts?content=52896") - modified to remove Arch + Weather sections, also changed MPD section to work with XMMS using xmmsctrl
**Tint:** [Tint Task Manager]("http://code.google.com/p/ttm/") - running at the bottom of the screen

I've just noticed that the themes *and* conky script are both from [**lyrae**]("http://www.gnome-look.org/usermanager/search.php?username=lyrae") so many thanks go out to her.

### Post by Nevon on 2008-03-09
> **rjmdomingo2003 said:**
> Have you tried offsetting them? Are you getting those by RSS?

Basically they're fetched directly from a website ([www.tv.nu](www.tv.nu)) through a python script. 
```
#!/usr/bin/python
# -*- coding: UTF-8 -*-
from urllib2 import urlopen
from BeautifulSoup import BeautifulSoup
url = "http://www.tv.nu/"

show_attrs = {"class": "po"}
topic_attrs = {"class": "tabla_topic"}
channel_classes = ["tabla_container", "tabla_container tcr"]

allowed_channels = ["SVT 1", "SVT 2", "TV3", "TV4", "TV5", "TV6", "MTV"]

for channel in BeautifulSoup(urlopen(url)).findAll("div"):

    if channel.has_key("class") and channel["class"] in channel_classes:

        topic = channel.find("div", topic_attrs)

        name = topic.p.string.strip()

        if name not in allowed_channels:
            continue

        print "Kanal: %s" % name

        this_show = None
        for show in channel.findAll("li", show_attrs):
            this_show = show
            this_time = this_show.contents[0].strip()
            this_name = this_show.a.string.strip()
            print "    Nu (%s): %s " % (this_time, this_name)

        if this_show:
            next_show = this_show.findNextSibling("li")
            if next_show:
                next_time = next_show.contents[0].strip()
                next_name = next_show.a.string.strip()
                print "    Next (%s): %s" % (next_time, next_name)
```

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-03-09
> **ayoli said:**
> would you mind sharing the conf (and maybe the icons that come with it ) ?
Sure. Fonts are linked as they can't be attached.
I use the if command to switch between interfaces and if the battery is charging or discharging (the icons work so well with it :)) A big thanks to Bruce about the align 2 so that the text doesn't move around.
```
background no
font Myraid Pro:size=7
use_xft yes
xftalpha 1.0
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window no
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
minimum_size 220 5
maximum_width 85 5
draw_shades no ### SHADOW ###
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes
default_outline_color white
default_color black ### Text Color ###
default_shade_color black
alignment bottom_right
gap_x 3
gap_y 3
no_buffers yes
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
uppercase yes

TEXT
   ${font StyleBats:size=18}4${font}${alignr 2}    ${time %I:%M}
   ${if_existing /sys/class/power_supply/BAT1/status Discharging}${font StyleBats:size=18}o${else}${font StyleBats:size=18}p${endif}${font}${alignr 2}    ${battery_percent BAT1}%
   ${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}M${font}${alignr 2}    ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}${upspeed eth0} Kb/s${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s${else}--${endif}${endif}
   ${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}S${font}${alignr 2}    ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}${downspeed eth0} Kb/s${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s${else}--${endif}${endif}
   ${font FreeSans:size=16}@${font}${alignr 2}    ${if_existing /sys/class/net/eth0/operstate up}${execi 300 python ~/.scripts/gmail.py}${else}${if_existing /sys/class/net/wlan0/operstate up}${execi 300 python ~/.scripts/gmail.py}${else}--${endif}${endif}
   ${font PizzaDude Bullets:size=16}]${font}${alignr 2}    ${texeci 10800 perl /home/shawn/.scripts/conky-updates.pl}
```

[http://www.dafont.com/fr/pizzadude-bullets.font](http://www.dafont.com/fr/pizzadude-bullets.font)
[http://www.dafont.com/style-bats.font](http://www.dafont.com/style-bats.font)

> **el mariachi said:**
> since we're speaking of ncmpc, is there a way to build random playlists?
It won't be random playlist, but if you throw on some tracks and press 'r', it goes to random mode of those tracks.

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2008-03-09
> **fedex1993 said:**
> like instead of green and black is there anyway to change it to like blue and black background and then the font is white so it goes along with my theme
I'll give you an old configuration. Put it in ~/.config/ncmpc if I remember right. Edit it to your needs.

```
list-format = "[%title%]"
status-format = "[%title%]"
xterm-title-format = "[%title%]"
set-xterm-title = yes
crossfade-time = 5
enable-mouse = no
enable-colors = yes
auto-center = yes
hide-cursor = 3

color background = none
color title = white
color title-bold = blue
color line = white
color line-flags = none
color list = white
color list-bold = blue
color progressbar = white
color status-state = white
color status-song = blue
color status-time = white
```

---

### Post by Yes on 2008-03-09
If you wanted it to be Artist - Song it would just be

```
list-format = "[%artist% - %title%]"
status-format = "[%artist% -%title%]"
xterm-title-format = "[%artist% -%title%]"
```

### Post by LeoSolaris on 2008-03-10
(Disclaimer to the mods: I am not 100% sure if this is the right area to post is question or not, so if I am wrong, I am sorry and please just move the thread to the proper place.)

I am still a relative newbie when it comes to Linux and Ubuntu, but so far I am definitely satisfied. I have been tweaking the way my desktop looks lately, and I would like to know what others have done to theirs.

Knock yourselves out and brag, I would like to know what sorts of tricks y'all have pulled to arrange your desktop to your liking. 

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/%5BIMG%5Dhttp://i97.photobucket.com/albums/l232/Leo_Solaris/Screenshot.png%5B/IMG%5D[/IMG][IMG]http://i97.photobucket.com/albums/l232/Leo_Solaris/Screenshot.png[/IMG]

My Gnome is relatively simple. I have a wallpaper from Socwall.com, my effects are customized, with a sky-domed background behind a spinning flat panel. (I decided to only use two desktops rather than the cubic four.)

I have an icon set called black-white 2 style (I would give the creator props, but it has been a while since I downloaded it and I forgot the creator's name, sorry!) The pointer if I remember is from the repo , actually. It's named Chameleon-pearl-small. 

The system monitor at the top is not the standard one either. It is currently tracking both processors, the memory, swap, and net transfer. The two squares next to the notify area are the two other partitions on my laptop, their from the repo as well.

The clock in the corner is a cario with ryx-glass theme that is set to start with the system, along with evolution.

The clock is a little bit misleading though. There are actually two of them there. One is a static that is set to stay under everything on all of the backgrounds, while the second, exactly the same is layed out over top, but as a widget layer, so I can push F9 at any time and "call" my clock to the surface. It's quite handy.

At the base is the by now standard AWN-dock. It's set with matching colors for the background, and the 3d glass look. It's set to hide behind windows so it is out of the way while working. I keep Swiftfox, the odd-looking Firefox button at the bottom, (You can Google for it. It's a really nice upgrade for Linux Firefox) Evolution, Tomboy Notes, Control Center, and the Terminal all on the dock.

Although you cannot see it in the picture, my window border is orbital from art.gnome.org. I synced up the rest of the colors on the windows to match the border for a smoother look. I added a background texture to nautilus as well, so the icons show up a little better.

I've had a blast tweaking the look for my Gnome, and I hope to get some ideas from the community for future mods.

Leo S.

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-03-10
> **RebounD11 said:**
> My first attempt at Fluxbox:

Can anyone tell me how to change the icon theme, not just the icons in the menu?

```
/home/daffy $ cat .gtkrc-2.0 
# -- THEME AUTO-WRITTEN DO NOT EDIT
include "/usr/share/themes/Mist/gtk-2.0/gtkrc"

include "/home/daffy/.gtkrc.mine"

# -- THEME AUTO-WRITTEN DO NOT EDIT

/home/daffy $ cat .gtkrc.mine 
gtk-icon-theme-name = "Neu"

```

### Post by Dr Small on 2008-03-10
> **fedex1993 said:**
> would really like to see your script that says dark ghost stuff and what not so, PLease oh yeah your desktop looks good
I spruced the script up before I read your post, but here it is with color!
```

#!/bin/bash

# A Simple Information Script
# which could be useful for screenshots.
# Simply edit the variables to change the values
# Any variable that is left blank will not show when executed.
#
# Usage: ./info
#
# Written by Dr Small
# http://php.8ez.com/drsmall/blog/

#Set your personal info here
#Anything that you leave unset will not display :)
email="drsmall@hackermail.com"
jabber="drsmall@cafelinux.com"
msn="drsmall@hackermail.com"
yahoo=""
icq="324-464-073"
gpg="26FD8AF9"
skype=""
aim=""
openid=""
launchpad="drsmall" #USERNAME ONLY
irc="DrSmall @ irc.freenode.net"
website="http://php.8ez.com/drsmall/blog/"

#Set your desktop config here
#Anything unset will not display.
desktop="IceWM"
theme="FauxGlass"
wallpaper="127.0.0.1"


#Some Additional Settings
#1 = true
#0 = false
show_user="1"
show_host="1"
prntscrn="0" #TAKE A SCREENSHOT
delay="5" #DELAY FOR SCREENSHOT, IN SECONDS



# There is nothing else to edit below here...


BLACK='\e[0;30m'
BLUE='\e[0;34m'
GREEN='\e[0;32m'
CYAN='\e[0;36m'
RED='\e[0;31m'
PURPLE='\e[0;35m'
BROWN='\e[0;33m'
LIGHTGRAY='\e[0;37m'
DARKGRAY='\e[1;30m'
LIGHTBLUE='\e[1;34m'
LIGHTGREEN='\e[1;32m'
LIGHTCYAN='\e[1;36m'
LIGHTRED='\e[1;31m'
LIGHTPURPLE='\e[1;35m'
YELLOW='\e[1;33m'
WHITE='\e[1;37m'
NC='\e[0m'


if [[ -z $* ]]; then

echo ''
	if [[ $show_user == "1" ]]; then

	echo -e $LIGHTCYAN 'User: '`whoami`

	fi

	if [[ $show_host == "1" ]]; then

	echo -e $YELLOW 'Host: '`hostname`

	fi

$0 --contact

echo  -e $NC ''
	if [[ -n $desktop ]]; then

	echo -e $LIGHTPURPLE 'Desktop: '$desktop

	fi

	if [[ -n $theme ]]; then

	echo -e $DARKGRAY 'Theme: '$theme

	fi

	if [[ -n $wallpaper ]]; then

	echo -e $GREEN 'Wallpaper: '$wallpaper $NC

	fi


echo ''

	if [[ $prntscrn == "1" ]]; then
	$0 --prntscrn
	fi
fi


if [[ $* == '--contact' || $* == '-c' ]]; then

echo ''

	if [[ -n $email ]]; then

	echo -e $BLUE 'Email:' $email
	
	fi

	if [[ -n $jabber ]]; then

	echo -e $GREEN 'Jabber:' $jabber

	fi

	if [[ -n $msn ]]; then

	echo -e $CYAN 'MSN:' $msn

	fi

	if [[ -n $yahoo ]]; then

	echo -e $RED 'Yahoo:' $yahoo
	
	fi

	if [[ -n $icq ]]; then

	echo -e $PURPLE 'ICQ #:' $icq

	fi

	if [[ -n $gpg ]]; then

	echo -e $LIGHTGRAY 'OpenPGP Key:' $gpg

	fi

	if [[ -n $skype ]]; then

	echo -e $DARKGREY 'Skype:' $skype

	fi

	if [[ -n $aim ]]; then

	echo -e $LIGHTBLUE 'AIM:' $aim

	fi

	if [[ -n $openid ]]; then

	echo -e $LIGHTGREEN 'OpenID:' $openid

	fi

	if [[ -n $launchpad ]]; then

	echo -e $LIGHTRED 'Launchpad: http://launchpad.net/~'$launchpad

	fi

	if [[ -n $irc ]]; then

	echo -e $LIGHTPURPLE 'IRC:' $irc

	fi

	if [[ -n $website ]]; then

	echo -e $BROWN 'Website:' $website

	fi
fi


if [[ $* == '--help' || $* == '-h' ]]; then
echo  -e $CYAN ''
echo -e 'Terminal Information... a useful tool for taking\nscreenshots'
echo ''
echo 'Help Contents:'
echo $0'  Executes the script.'
echo $0' -c'
echo $0' --contact  Only displays the contact information.'
echo $0' -p'
echo $0' --prntscrn  Only used if $prntscrn variable is set.'
echo $0' -h'
echo $0' --help  Displays this message.'
echo ''
echo -e 'For this script to function properly,\nPlease edit the variables in the file\nto show the correct information.\n\nIf you wish for a certain variable\nto not show up, just simply leave it empty.'
echo -e $NC ''

fi

if [[ $* == "--prntscrn" || $* == "-p" ]]; then
scrot -d $delay
fi

exit

```

---

### Post by raul_ on 2008-03-12
> **ayoli said:**
> Have a look to [this post]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=711179&page=32#312"), it's the same config

It's not quite the same. I grabbed one of my old ones, changed the fonts and added weather support with the pogodynka script

```
own_window yes
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
use_xft yes
update_interval 5
draw_shades no
draw_borders no
xftfont Calibri:pixelsize=13
minimum_size 1280 0
border_margin 20
default_color ffffff
alignment top_left
gap_x 1080
gap_y 42
use_spacer no

TEXT



${offset -45}${voffset -10}${font weather:size=40} ${execi 300 /home/raul/.scripts/conditions.sh}${voffset -5}${font Myriad Pro:size=8}${time %b. %d } ${time %H:%M}
${offset 43}${voffset -45}Lisboa, PT   ${execi 300 /home/raul/.scripts/pogodynka.sh} ºC



${font StyleBats:size=25}a${font Myriad Pro:size=8}Cpu ${cpu}% ${acpitemp}C


${font StyleBats:size=20}c${font Myriad Pro:size=8}Ram ${memperc}% | Swap ${swapperc}%


${font StyleBats:size=20}o${font Myriad Pro:size=8}Down: ${downspeed wlan0}Kb/s | Up: ${upspeed wlan0}Kb/s


${font StyleBats:size=20}b${font Myriad Pro:size=8}Battery: ${battery BAT0} ${battery_time BAT0}
```

you should read the scripts (not really pogodynka, i think it's in polish) to know what paths to change, and you should go to weather.com, enter your city, and copy the code in the URL to the pogodynka.sh file, where mine is right now (unless your interested in knowing the weather in Lisbon)

### Post by klange on 2008-03-12
> **Hells_Dark said:**
> Could you share the script ?
Nice one :)

It's not quite done yet
```
#!/bin/bash
# Super Duper Screenshot Script

# Clean Wallpapers...
compiz-send-event core show_desktop_key
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_1_key
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_1.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_2_key
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_2.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_3_key        
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_3.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_4_key
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_4.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
sleep 2
scrot expo_clean.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
sleep 2
# Dirty Workspaces...
compiz-send-event core show_desktop_key
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_1_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_1.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_2_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_2.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_3_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_3.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_4_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_4.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
sleep 2
scrot expo_dirty.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
cp *.png thumbs/
cd thumbs
mogrify -format png -thumbnail 200 *.png
for i in *.png; do
rot=0
let "rot = $RANDOM % 20 - 10"
convert $i \
          -bordercolor white  -border 6 \
          -bordercolor grey60 -border 1 \
          -background  none   -rotate $rot \
          -background  black  \( +clone -shadow 60x4+4+4 \) +swap \
          -background  none   -flatten \
          -depth 8  -quality 95   $i
done
cd ..
for i in *.png; do
echo -n "[[img]http://YOUR WEBSITE/workstation/$DIR/thumbs/$i[/img]](\"http://YOUR WEBSITE/$DIR/$i\") "
done
```

Still have to add some cube pics and do something to force my Cairo-dock to show. I have Fade Desktop enabled as it forces all windows to hide / show when Ctrl+Alt+D is pressed, unlike the standard behavior. You'll need ImageMagick to use the thumbnail parts. 'compiz-send-event' is [this Python script](http://forum.compiz-fusion.org/showthread.php?t=7359). Lastly, make sure that you have a 'thumbs' directory in whatever folder you put it in.

My Expo shots:
[[img]http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/march_12/thumbs/expo_clean.png[/img]]("http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/march_12/expo_clean.png") [[img]http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/march_12/thumbs/expo_dirty.png[/img]]("http://random.ogunderground.com/workstation/march_12/expo_dirty.png")

### Post by bobdob20 on 2008-03-13
> **miggys said:**
> bobdob, or anyone else who knows, how'd you get 12 hour clock in ncmpc?
Thanks!

hey, just change the screen_clock.c to this and compile from source.

```
/*
 * $Id: screen_clock.c 2668 2004-11-15 11:23:11Z kaw $
 *
 * This file is based on the 'Grand digital clock' (gdc.c) shipped with 
 * ncurses. 
 */

#include <time.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <glib.h>
#include <ncurses.h>

#include "config.h"

#ifndef  DISABLE_CLOCK_SCREEN
#include "ncmpc.h"
#include "mpdclient.h"
#include "options.h"
#include "command.h"
#include "screen.h"
#include "screen_utils.h"

#define YDEPTH	5
#define BUFSIZE 64

#define ENABLE_SECONDS 0
#define ENABLE_12HOUR 1

static window_t win = { NULL, 0, 0 };
static gboolean enable_seconds = ENABLE_SECONDS;

/* orginal variables from gdc.c */
static short disp[11] =
{
    075557, 011111, 071747, 071717, 055711,
    074717, 074757, 071111, 075757, 075717, 002020
};

static long older[6], next[6], newer[6], mask;

static int YBASE = 10;
static int XBASE = 10;
static int XLENGTH = 54;


/* orginal functions */
static void
set(int t, int n)
{
  int i, m;

  m = 7 << n;
  for (i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
    next[i] |= ((disp[t] >> ((4 - i) * 3)) & 07) << n;
    mask |= (next[i] ^ older[i]) & m;
  }
  if (mask & m)
    mask |= m;
}

static void
drawbox(void)
{
  chtype bottom[XLENGTH + 2];
  int n;

  mvwaddch(win.w, YBASE - 1, XBASE - 2, ACS_ULCORNER);
  whline(win.w, ACS_HLINE, XLENGTH + 1);
  mvwaddch(win.w, YBASE - 1, XBASE + XLENGTH, ACS_URCORNER);

  mvwaddch(win.w, YBASE + YDEPTH, XBASE - 2, ACS_LLCORNER);
  mvwinchnstr(win.w, YBASE + YDEPTH, XBASE, bottom, XLENGTH);
  for (n = 0; n <= XLENGTH; n++)
    bottom[n] = ACS_HLINE | (bottom[n] & (A_ATTRIBUTES | A_COLOR));
  mvwaddchnstr(win.w, YBASE + YDEPTH, XBASE -1, bottom, XLENGTH + 1);
  mvwaddch(win.w, YBASE + YDEPTH, XBASE + XLENGTH, ACS_LRCORNER);
  
  wmove(win.w, YBASE, XBASE - 2);
  wvline(win.w, ACS_VLINE, YDEPTH);
  
  wmove(win.w, YBASE, XBASE + XLENGTH);
  wvline(win.w, ACS_VLINE, YDEPTH);
}


static void
standt(int on)
{
  if(on)
    wattron(win.w, A_REVERSE);
  else
    wattroff(win.w, A_REVERSE);
}



/* ncmpc screen functions */

static void
clock_resize(int cols, int rows)
{
  int j;
  
  for (j = 0; j < 5; j++)
    older[j] = newer[j] = next[j] = 0;

  win.cols = cols;
  win.rows = rows;
  
  if( cols<60 )
    enable_seconds = FALSE;
  else
    enable_seconds = ENABLE_SECONDS;

  if( enable_seconds )
    XLENGTH = 54;
  else
    XLENGTH = 54-18;

  
  XBASE = (cols-XLENGTH)/2;
  YBASE = (rows-YDEPTH)/2-(YDEPTH/2)+2;
}

static void 
clock_init(WINDOW *w, int cols, int rows)
{
  win.w = w;
  clock_resize(cols, rows);
}

static void 
clock_exit(void)
{
}

static void 
clock_open(screen_t *screen, mpdclient_t *c)
{
  int j;

  for (j = 0; j < 5; j++)
    older[j] = newer[j] = next[j] = 0;

}

static void 
clock_close(void)
{
}

static char *
clock_title(char *str, size_t size)
{
  return _("Clock");
}

static void 
clock_update(screen_t *screen, mpdclient_t *c)
{  
  time_t now;
  struct tm *tm;
  long t, a;
  int i, j, s, k;
  char buf[BUFSIZE];
  bool am;
  char AM[] = {"AM"};
  char PM[] = {"PM"};

  time(&now);
  tm = localtime(&now);

  /* set clock to 12 hour */
  if (ENABLE_12HOUR)
    {
       if (tm->tm_hour < 12) am = true;
       else am = false;

       if (tm->tm_hour > 12) tm->tm_hour -= 12;
       if (tm->tm_hour == 0) tm->tm_hour = 12;
    }


  if( win.rows<=YDEPTH+1 || win.cols<=XLENGTH+1 )
    {
      strftime(buf, BUFSIZE, "%X ",tm);
      mvwaddstr(win.w, win.rows ? win.rows/2:0, (win.cols-strlen(buf))/2, buf);
      wrefresh(win.w);
      return;
    }

  
  mask = 0;
  set(tm->tm_sec % 10, 0);
  set(tm->tm_sec / 10, 4);
  set(tm->tm_min % 10, 10);
  set(tm->tm_min / 10, 14);
  set(tm->tm_hour % 10, 20);
  set(tm->tm_hour / 10, 24);
  set(10, 7);
  set(10, 17);

  for (k = 0; k < 6; k++) {
    newer[k] = (newer[k] & ~mask) | (next[k] & mask);
    next[k] = 0;
    for (s = 1; s >= 0; s--) {
      standt(s);
      for (i = 0; i < 6; i++) {
	if ((a = (newer[i] ^ older[i]) & (s ? newer : older)[i])
	    != 0) {
	  for (j = 0, t = 1 << 26; t; t >>= 1, j++) {
	    if (a & t) {
	      if (!(a & (t << 1))) {
		wmove(win.w, YBASE + i, XBASE + 2 * j);
	      }
	      if( enable_seconds || j<18 )
		waddstr(win.w, "  ");
	    }
	  }
	}
	if (!s) {
	  older[i] = newer[i];
	}
      }
      if (!s) {
	wrefresh(win.w);
      }
    }
  }
  
#ifdef HAVE_LOCALE_H
  strftime(buf, BUFSIZE, "%x", tm);
# else
  /* this depends on the detailed format of ctime(3) */
  strcpy(buf, ctime(&now));
  strcpy(buf + 10, buf + 19);
#endif
  mvwaddstr(win.w, YBASE+YDEPTH+1, (win.cols-strlen(buf))/2 - 1, buf);

  /* displays AM/PM */
  if (ENABLE_12HOUR)
    {
      if (am == true) strcpy(buf, AM);
      else  strcpy(buf, PM);
      if (ENABLE_SECONDS)
      mvwaddstr(win.w, YBASE+YDEPTH-1, (win.cols-strlen(buf))/2 - 10, buf);
      else
      mvwaddstr(win.w, YBASE+YDEPTH-1, (win.cols-strlen(buf))/2 - 1, buf);
    }
  
  wmove(win.w, 6, 0);
  drawbox();
  wrefresh(win.w);
}

static void 
clock_paint(screen_t *screen, mpdclient_t *c)
{
  /* this seems to be a better way to clear the window than wclear() ?! */
  wmove(win.w, 0, 0);
  wclrtobot(win.w);
  clock_update(screen, c);
}



static int 
clock_cmd(screen_t *screen, mpdclient_t *c, command_t cmd)
{
  return 0;
}


screen_functions_t *
get_screen_clock(void)
{
  static screen_functions_t functions;

  memset(&functions, 0, sizeof(screen_functions_t));
  functions.init   = clock_init;
  functions.exit   = clock_exit;
  functions.open   = clock_open;
  functions.close  = clock_close;
  functions.resize = clock_resize;
  functions.paint  = clock_paint;
  functions.update = clock_update;
  functions.cmd    = clock_cmd;
  functions.get_lw = NULL;
  functions.get_title = clock_title;

  return &functions;
}


#endif
```

12 hour is enabled by default, but can be disabled by setting ENABLE_12HOUR to 0. It should also work with seconds enabled. Hope that helps.

### Post by markp1989 on 2008-03-13
> **WindowsSucks said:**
> It's not quite done yet
```
#!/bin/bash
# Super Duper Screenshot Script

# Clean Wallpapers...
compiz-send-event core show_desktop_key
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_1_key
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_1.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_2_key
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_2.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_3_key        
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_3.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_4_key
sleep 2
scrot wallpaper_4.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
sleep 2
scrot expo_clean.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
sleep 2
# Dirty Workspaces...
compiz-send-event core show_desktop_key
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_1_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_1.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_2_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_2.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_3_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_3.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event rotate rotate_to_4_key
sleep 2
scrot workspace_4.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
sleep 2
scrot expo_dirty.png
sleep 1
compiz-send-event expo expo_key
cp *.png thumbs/
cd thumbs
mogrify -format png -thumbnail 200 *.png
for i in *.png; do
rot=0
let "rot = $RANDOM % 20 - 10"
convert $i \
          -bordercolor white  -border 6 \
          -bordercolor grey60 -border 1 \
          -background  none   -rotate $rot \
          -background  black  \( +clone -shadow 60x4+4+4 \) +swap \
          -background  none   -flatten \
          -depth 8  -quality 95   $i
done
cd ..
for i in *.png; do
echo -n "[[img]http://YOUR WEBSITE/workstation/$DIR/thumbs/$i[/img]](\"http://YOUR WEBSITE/$DIR/$i\") "
done
```

Still have to add some cube pics and do something to force my Cairo-dock to show. I have Fade Desktop enabled as it forces all windows to hide / show when Ctrl+Alt+D is pressed, unlike the standard behavior. You'll need ImageMagick to use the thumbnail parts. 'compiz-send-event' is [this Python script](http://forum.compiz-fusion.org/showthread.php?t=7359). Lastly, make sure that you have a 'thumbs' directory in whatever folder you put it in.

### Post by klange on 2008-03-13
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Done!
Nice!
This 8-image limit is really a pain... I made some changes to my script to allow easy access to the thumbnail and post generator so I can add new pics easily and then just recreate the thumbs.

### Post by cawill on 2008-03-14
> **dinasty said:**
> How'd you get the close, minimize and restore buttons on the right side instead of left wich is default for Elegant britt?
would be really nice to know, been trying to find that out for several days now :D

Open Emerald Theme Manager > Edit Themes > Titlebar,

Then Edit Title-bar Object Layout,

Hope this helps, Chris.

### Post by BluntBox on 2008-03-15
> **dinasty said:**
> How'd you get the close, minimize and restore buttons on the right side instead of left wich is default for Elegant britt?
would be really nice to know, been trying to find that out for several days now :D

Open Emerald Theme Manager, and head to Edit Theme, then Titlebar. On the right side is a dropdown box with a couple of preset layouts, or you can write your own using the info below the box.

### Post by abhinandh on 2008-03-17
> **chick said:**
> Conky? Mind posting your script?

```

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background yes

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont OBHandel:size=9

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 1.0

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes

# If own_window is yes, you may use type normal, desktop or override
own_window_type normal

# Use pseudo transparency with own_window?
own_window_transparent yes

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 180 2


# Maximum width
maximum_width 400

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Draw borders around graphs
draw_graph_borders no

# Stippled borders?
# stippled_borders 8

# border margins
# border_margin 2

# border width
# border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color black
default_shade_color red
default_outline_color green

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
#alignment none

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 40
gap_y 350

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale no

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

#  unused text
#  Current:${alignr}${execi 20 /home/tonyt/scripts/.conky_eth2} Mbits/sec
#  hda Temp:${alignr}${execi 1800 /home/tonyt/scripts/.hdtemp}

TEXT
Ubuntu 7.10 $machine

Uptime $alignr$uptime
Hard Drive Temp $alignr${execi 300 nc localhost 7634 | cut -c21-22;} C
System Temp $alignr${execi 60 sensors *-isa-0680|grep temp2| cut -c15-16;} C

$processes Processes($running_processes Running)

CPU1 $alignr${cpu cpu1}% 
${color #8c8c8c}${cpubar cpu1}$color

CPU2 $alignr${cpu cpu2}% 
${color #8c8c8c}${cpubar cpu2}$color

MEM  $alignc $mem/1GiB $alignr${memperc}% 
${color #8c8c8c}$membar$color

/ $alignc$fs_used/$fs_size$alignr${fs_used_perc /}% 
${color #8c8c8c}${fs_bar /}$color

Swap $alignc$swap/$swapmax$alignr$swapperc% 
${color #8c8c8c}$swapbar$color

```

and that script is configured for 2 cpu's.

[[IMG]http://i193.photobucket.com/albums/z150/wfgeppetto/th_scrnsht2.png[/IMG]](http://i193.photobucket.com/albums/z150/wfgeppetto/scrnsht2.png)
[[IMG]http://i193.photobucket.com/albums/z150/wfgeppetto/th_scrnsht1.png[/IMG]](http://i193.photobucket.com/albums/z150/wfgeppetto/scrnsht1.png)

The wallpaper is available at daim.org.
The color theme is entirely custom
The icon set is Kreski lines.
Everything else is readily available in the Art Manager.
Compiz has nearly all the plugins installed, 3dwindows is what makes them pop up off the cube.
I don't run screenlets, they slow my poor little laptop down too much.
The dock is Avant-window-navigator, with AWN curves installed.
I don't use skybox, because I haven't found an image that I like for it.

> Ok so I tried changing from Elegant Brit to another GTK theme, and something went terribly wrong. It seems that my panel, Nautilus, Firefox, etc, are all stuck in Elegant Brit like shown in the screenshot.
Check your gtkrc.mine etc. for any traces of it. Those will override it.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-03-19
> **sunexplodes said:**
> Ah, perfect, I'll add the link to my post. 

Thanks a lot, I'll have to dig backward and see what your current desk looks like.. Also, have you ever considered a dark version of elegant brit? It looks so great, but it's just so WHITE. ;)

My current desktop is wearing all things Elegant Brit... GTK, Xfwm4, wallpapers, splash screens, etc... It's a way to test it and make sure it's good enough for other people to use it as well. But I'm thinking about doing another theme, I'm just not sure of what will it be. I need to do something different after all this time breathing Elegant Brit day and night, but then again I know it would be interesting to do a dark version of it. I've been also thinking of something with fresh colours, something to celebrate Spring, you know... "Elegant-like" or not, that is the question... Meanwhile, Ayoli made a great mod of EB in blue, and a darker tone of gray. I recommend it if you want to give it a try. However, I know you're actually interested in a black/dark-gray theme, from what I see in your desktops, so I'll think about it...

I like to make graphics, to design, etc... It's something that always interested me, but that I never had a way to express (no academical education either, etc.)... Linux was my first outlet. And it's being cool so far!

EDIT: I've been also thinking about doing a theme in warm colours which would be, well, dedicated to Ubuntu... It really NEEDS something beautiful as a default. But of course, pixmap themes will never make it; I'm aware any distro would prefer something built up with Clearlooks, Murrina, etc... Anyway. It's also something I think about.

### Post by graabein on 2008-03-20
My Xfce on Xubuntu 7.10 with Quod Libet and PCManFM running.

Just found the [applecure GTK2 theme]("http://www.xfce-look.org/content/show.php/show.php?content=76899") and it's fantastic. It requires the pixmap engine from the repositories and the Aurora GTK engine ([link]("http://linux.softpedia.com/progDownload/Aurora-Gtk-Engine-Download-32542.html")). 

Icons are nuoveXT.2.2. Background is some old MAC wallpaper, I think it's called aqua graphite or something.

[[IMG]http://img297.imageshack.us/img297/4942/200803201117311280x1024dp3.th.png[/IMG]](http://img297.imageshack.us/my.php?image=200803201117311280x1024dp3.png)

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-03-23
> **i.wanna.corndog said:**
> I love that theme! Could you link to it?

EDIT: Also, I'm a bit new to Ubuntu and am not quite familiar with some of the software involved in many of these themes. When you say that it is Xfce and GTK+ 2, do I need to install those to get that theme to work (I'm assuming)? Are there any good threads I could read about the different desktop environments and how to install them?

Thanks!

Hello there!

Differently from other operating systems, the GNU/Linux systems like Ubuntu don't have only one desktop environment available, as you already understood. Besides, the windows' controls are not attached to just one window manager (to explain it very roughly, a window manager takes care of the borders of the applications, the titles, the maximize/minimize/close buttons, etc.). So you have different full desktop environments, like GNOME, KDE or Xfce, but tons of different window managers at your choice, like Metacity (GNOME's default), KWin (KDE's default), Xfwm4 (Xfce's default), Openbox, Fluxbox, Compiz-Fusion with Emerald, etc. And you can do some mixes as you please, with the required hacks. 

Basically, if you're using the regular Ubuntu, then you're using GNOME, and therefore you already have the required GTK+ libraries installed in your PC. Lots of applications are based on GTK libraries; a basic user probably won't need to use QT apps if KDE isn't installed, but there is no problem in installing, say, Amarok for a nice music player or K3B to burn CDs and DVDs, because Ubuntu (and other Linux systems) will take care of the necessary QT libraries to have KDE apps running.

In the Ubuntu world, you can easily install Xfce or KDE, through the packages xubuntu-desktop (for Xfce) or kubuntu-desktop (for KDE). Several window managers are also available for installation.

The fact that I'm using Xfce does not mean that you, on GNOME, cannot use the theme. That is why it's a GTK theme. It does not depend on a specific desktop environment. It works with all GTK apps, whether they are working on a GNOME environment, on Xfce or on any other. The same goes for QT themes, for KDE applications, running in every environment. Of course, there are themes specifically for Emerald, for Xfwm4, for Openbox, for Metacity, etc. But Elegant Brit, and all GTK themes, are usable whenever there is a GTK app. 

In your case, assuming you're in GNOME, there is the regular GTK theme you can use and also a Metacity theme. If you're using Compiz, there is also an Emerald version of Elegant Brit (and of lots of themes, of course). I hope this explanation wasn't too confuse.

Meanwhile, as for this dark theme I made, I still haven't uploaded it to the OpenDesktop.org websites (that is, GNOME-Look.org, Xfce-Look.org, etc.), as this was a very frantic day to me, but I'll do it as soon as possible. Sorry for the delay. I (and the community) am here to help in what is possible.

P.S.: It's online: [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Elegant+Mine?content=77491](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Elegant+Mine?content=77491)

---

Based in Clearlooks with different window borders. I am using SystemGX for the window borders, and UltimateGnome for the icons.
The desktop background is a slightly edited Hardy default wallpaper. For once, I decided to go with a blue theme, rather than orange or black which is what I usually do. This is also the first time in ages that I haven't used some form of digitally manipulated plant photo as my wallpaper.
The fonts used are: AnjaliOldLipi for applications, Sans for documents and desktop, Sans Bold for window borders, and Andale Mono for monospace.

### Post by Mazza558 on 2008-03-23
In my continuous search for gnome desktop theming perfection, I think I may have just about found it. I was beginning to get sick of non-unified (but good) themes, and a lucky chance allowed me to find 2 perfect themes...

This is my desktop at the moment:

[[IMG]http://img529.imageshack.us/img529/5387/desky1py7.th.png[/IMG]](http://img529.imageshack.us/my.php?image=desky1py7.png)

Sure, this looks nice, but look closer... a well-polished theme really does work wonders...

Perfect Tooltips:

[IMG]http://img218.imageshack.us/img218/7638/tooltipbx2.png[/IMG]

Smooth dialog boxes:

[IMG]http://img229.imageshack.us/img229/4512/uploadyi5.png[/IMG]


The theme uses:

-AWN
-Clearlooks
-Gommoso Emerald theme [(click here)]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Gommoso?content=75530")
-Crashbit Icon theme[(click here)]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/CrashBit?content=71140")

Overall, I think I can show this theme to anyone who thinks Linux does not have an original and great theme. I think it looks slightly similar to the 2003 "longhorn" look which was originally going to be Vista (but abandoned), and all I really need now is a nice wallpaper to match. It goes completely against the glassy/metallic looks of OSX and Vista. Kudos to all the people involved in the projects mentioned above!

### Post by Mr. Picklesworth on 2008-03-23
For those who don't want to bother with Emerald (eg: Using Hardy with Metacity's fancy new compositing), the Metacity theme Plano looks similarly nice:
[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Plano?content=76825](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Plano?content=76825)
No blue highlight at the top, but it also aims to blend perfectly with the GTK theme.

We seem to have conjured up personal favourite desktops at the same time! Mine (at long last!) is attached (although I have added titles back to the windows since).
Borderless windows really open up the visuals, I think. That way, a beautiful interface (like we have with these here forums!) is not closed up inside an obtrusive window but instead stretches to the furthest reaches it can.

Some may say "Mac-ish", but that's really not the case. Apple doesn't have the guts to kill off the redundant window Close and Minimize buttons! Besides which, the only thing Mac-like here is a silver gradient for the title bar, and that really is just any gradient blending with the GTK theme. It *does* look unusually attractive, though.

How did you get that nice looking semi-transparent panel background *with* a gradient?

---

Awesome. Where can I get all this? :P
