### Post by Mr. Picklesworth on 2008-03-24
> **herbster said:**
> [[img]http://www.bobgill.net/desktop032308_thumb.jpg[/img]](http://www.bobgill.net/desktop032308.jpg)

[[img]http://www.bobgill.net/desktop032308busy_thumb.jpg[/img]](http://www.bobgill.net/desktop032308busy.jpg)

Herbster, I want your computer.

> **mrgnash said:**
> Awesome. Where can I get all this? :P

Have to admit, most of it is just defaults. Using the new Clearlooks engine from Gnome 2.22 for the attractive smooth edges (the Human-Clearlooks theme). Err, disclaimer: Don't run Hardy on a production machine, however beautiful it may be. Human may give better results with Gutsy, since the gradient is, this time, a bad thing...

What I wanted to show off with that screenshot is how much difference just the Metacity theme can make. Ubuntu's defaults could do with a bigger focus on that.

Most of the attractive themes posted here have a big thing going with window decorations, and that more often than not involves trimming them out as opposed to pushing them in. The visible end of windows should not act like prisons for their content, but little helpers that work to make that content readable. Helpers do not impose themselves, but add to what's important: Friendly harmony, in this case with GTK. For example, drop shadows and title bars (permitting the user to easily position that content) really help to tie up loose edges around GTK on its own. Flashy, orange title bars and solid, thick borders that add a completely different stroke to the theme do not.

My desktop, in general:

-To customize window buttons, go to Configuration Editor (gconf-editor). Go to apps/metacity/general (just search for Metacity and you'll be there). Edit the key button_layout to your heart's content. ":" divides left and right, and the system panics if it is not there. Mine is "menu:" If you are running Hardy or anything else with GNOME 2.22, check the box for "compositing_manager".

-My panel background gradient is attached. (Best way to reproduce: Open GIMP, create a gradient from white to the default solid colour of your panel right now as grabbed via a colour picker). Simply drag and drop the image to your panel and it should apply. (Or do it the boring way in the panel's Properties). Mine is tailored for a panel positioned on the top with size of 30px.

-Link to Plano was posted before, but [here it is](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Plano?content=76825) again.

-The background I have there is the one included with the Hardy beta... The thing with this is that it really flows well with practically any GTK theme you have right now (taking no credit for that perfection!) except for the panel, so there is no one perfect background. Still, it does look great with the green meadow background in the package [gnome-backgrounds](apt://gnome-backgrounds).

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-03-25
> **raul_ said:**
> ++

Finally went through the long list of messages. Sorry, guys.

[QUOTE=days_of_ruin]Would it be possible to have emerald enable for one user and
metacity for another?[/QUOTE]

Clearly. That is why you have a different Home folder for each user. The thing is that each Home stores the preferences for its own user, so one can decide to have Metacity on his GNOME session and another can decide to have Emerald enabled. Just like each one can have different themes, icons, wallpapers, etc.

### Post by urukrama on 2008-03-26
> **el mariachi said:**
> uuuuuuuu! Urukrama! we were all wondering when you'd show up :D
welcome back! :3

Thank you. Good to see you are still here too :)

> **el mariachi said:**
> 
oh: request: your PS1 line please :P
(yeah I should be the one giving a welcome back gift I know heh)

Sure, here it is:

```
BGREEN='\[\033[1;32m\]'
GREEN='\[\033[0;32m\]'
BRED='\[\033[1;31m\]'
RED='\[\033[0;31m\]'
BBLUE='\[\033[1;34m\]'
BLUE='\[\033[0;34m\]'
NORMAL='\[\033[00m\]'
PS1="${NORMAL}[${NORMAL}\h${NORMAL}] ${NORMAL}\w ${RED}\$ ${NORMAL}"
```

I use red, but adjust my Xfce-terminal preferences to display orange instead of red so I can have orange in ncmpc as well.

### Post by RebounD11 on 2008-03-26
> **xThUnDeR8600 said:**
> how do you get that system info thing on your desktop like that

That's conky... install it and modify it's config file... it could be in your home dir .conkyrc, or in /etc/conky/conky.conf or you can just make one and run conky with 

```
conky -c config_file_path
```

I'll attach mine if I can find it... I think I have two variants... and btw I lost my audacious script... the one I use to get that progress bar... I'll try to write it again but maybe later. 
 
I'm up to my neck in work now so maybe during this night (it's already 11:40PM here in Romania)

EDIT: Or you could go to to this thread [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=4586739](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=4586739)

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2008-03-28
I'll post my conkyrc from my previous post..for those who want to cannibalize it :)

own_window no
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
use_xft yes
update_interval 0.5
draw_shades no
draw_borders no
xftfont HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:pixelsize=12
minimum_size 1280 0
border_margin 1
default_color 9d9d9d
alignment top_left
gap_x 1130
gap_y 30
use_spacer no

TEXT
${time %b}
${voffset -7}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=16}${time %d}
${offset 25}${voffset -38}${color c90006}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=26.7}${execi 100 /home/melski/scripts/weather/pogodynka.sh | cut -c1-4}${offset -3}C
${offset -2}${voffset -20}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=47}${time %I}
${offset 77}${voffset -100}${color 9d9d9d}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=18.2}${time %M}
${offset 77}${voffset -12}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=15.65}${time %p}

### Post by new2*buntu on 2008-03-28
I know that I have posted a screenshot earlier this month, but I am posting this because I think it looks better. Also, many of the screenshots in this thread are quite nice, so I hope this one is not that bad... any comments or suggestions are appreciated.

> 
March 28, 2008 Theme Details:
GTK Theme: MurrinaWhite, from gnome-look.org
Metacity Theme: Blended Small, from gnome-look.org
Icon Theme: CrashBit, also from gnome-look.org
Wallpaper: Candido no text, from candido.berlios.de 
XMMS Theme: TiAmp, again from gnome-look.org 
Nautilus Background: Wavy White, from the default selection
Desktop Font: Transformers Solid Normal size 10, from the fun fonts 
package, which can be found at gnome-look.org
Metacity Window Border Font: Star Vader Size 9, also from fun fonts
Application Font: DejaVu Sans Book size 10
Document Font: Liberation Sans size 10
Fixed Width (Terminal) Font: Monospace size 10
Other Information: I am running Gnome 2.22 on Debian Testing (currently 
named 'Lenny'), with the built-in Metacity compositing turned on. Also, 
I am using Linux Kernel 2.22-3-686, although I have kernel 2.24-1-686 
installed, because the wireless drivers I am using are still on the 
2.22-3-686 version package.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-03-31
I'm really loving the Artwiz fonts so much... The only problem I had, since I'm Portuguese and my desktop is in my language, were some "special" characters with accents. However, today I found a ISO-8859-1 set of Artwiz fonts on Sourceforge which works marvelously. In case someone wants it, it's on the following link: [http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=170423](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=170423)

This is not a screenshot, but it might be helpful to other users anyway. I just copied the fonts inside of the pack to my /usr/share/fonts/X11/misc folder, replaced the old ones, restarted X (doing sudo fc-cache -fv wasn't enough) and voilà. Cool.

---

### Post by ayoli on 2008-03-31
> **What is in a name? said:**

However, today I found a ISO-8859-1 set of Artwiz fonts on Sourceforge which works marvelously. In case someone wants it, it's on the following link: [http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=170423](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=170423)

This is not a screenshot, but it might be helpful to other users anyway. I just copied the fonts inside of the pack to my /usr/share/fonts/X11/misc folder, replaced the old ones, restarted X (doing sudo fc-cache -fv wasn't enough) and voilà. Cool.

### Post by -Phi- on 2008-03-31
> **crocowhile said:**
> about this [screenshot]("http://ebupof.deviantart.com/art/My-Desktop-080229-78734750"):
